Current Events Commentary

Significant Attention Should Be Paid to the Inner Mongolia Problem

— Li

Recent domestic and international telegrams have conveyed a tendency towards normalized Sino-Japanese diplomacy. However, the situation in Inner Mongolia is worsening. This is a problem that cannot be ignored.

According to the Tanaka Memorial, "To conquer China, we must first conquer Manchuria and Mongolia. To conquer the world, we must first conquer China." "Use the rights in Manchuria and Mongolia as the command tower, seize all of China's resources, and then use China's resources to conquer the islands of Southeast Asia, Central and Small Asia, and Europe." It is evident that our Manchuria and Mongolia were long in the minds of the Continental Policy advocates, and conquering Manchuria and Mongolia was a necessary stage in completing the Continental Policy. "After the September 18th Incident, the Continental Policy advocates not only realized their great desire to conquer Manchuria, but also divided the Horqin League, Josutu League, and Jolim League, which straddled the four provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Jehol in Inner Mongolia, into four Xing'an Provinces." As a result, the Xilingol League, Ulanqab League, and Ih Ju League from Chahar-Suiyuan to Gansu-Ningxia felt a sense of imminent danger. In the spring of this year, the puppet army of Li Shou-hsin occupied the six counties of Guyuan, Baochang, Kangbao, Zhangbei, Gaodu, and Huade in the Xilingol League of northern Chahar, offering the great granary of northern Kou and the great pasture of northern Chahar to the Continental Policy advocates. Within a week of Shangdu's fall, the puppet army invaded the Ulanqab League in eastern Suiyuan. Fortunately, the Jin-Sui troops had made early arrangements and were prepared, and their attempt was not realized.

However, to complete their policy, the Continental Policy advocates must occupy the entire Inner Mongolia. For the past six months, they have been appeasing feudal princes on the one hand and actively preparing militarily on the other. Therefore, in the Chahar-Mongolia area, not only did the assassination of Mongolian Central Committee member Ni Guanzhou and the departure from the temple of Yun Jixian, the section chief of the Security Department of the Mongolian Political Council, occur, but also the Shangdu airfield was completed, and special agencies in various banners of Gansu-Ningxia were successively established.

The princes and nobles of various leagues and banners in Suiyuan and Mongolia are well aware of the difficulties faced by Chahar-Mongolia. They previously appealed to the Central Government, requesting permission to form another political committee, under the guidance of the Central Government, to govern autonomously in separate districts from Chahar-Mongolia and to unite to save the nation. The Central Government approved their request and specially allowed them to organize the Suiyuan Mongolian Political Council to govern Suiyuan and Mongolia. This popular self-awareness movement has great significance for our national defense. However, administrative measures alone cannot stop the Continental Policy advocates' coveting of the entire Inner Mongolia. Recently, the puppet regime drove a large number of bandits to attack Suiyuan and Mongolia. Rebel troops in the West Sunid Banner of the Ulanqab League in Suiyuan and Mongolia prevented Shi Wang from returning to his post. Civil unrest was brewing in the Ih Ju League. And De Wang, the chairman of the Chahar-Mongolia Political Council, was assassinated in Bailingmiao. These events, happening one after another, who can believe that they have nothing to do with the Continental Policy advocates? Now the bandit troops invading Suiyuan have been repelled, and Shi Wang has been escorted back to his banner by Fu Zuoyi, the chairman of Suiyuan. However, the hidden worries of Inner Mongolia will not be eliminated. Once the entire Inner Mongolia is lost, not only will the Northwest lose its buffer, but also the Yellow River basin will be in imminent danger. This is something we must pay close attention to. British General Harding Newman said, "To strive for national survival, we must use various methods and cooperate at the same time to achieve our goals." We sincerely hope that the central and local authorities will quickly develop various appropriate methods and implement them at the same time, so that the entire Inner Mongolia will not become a continuation of the four northeastern provinces.

The Japanese Ambassador to Russia Reports on the Current Situation in Soviet Russia and Makes Important Recommendations to Foreign Minister Arita, Saying That the Military Strength Stationed in Manchuria Must Be Increased to Confront It

(Tokyo) The Ambassador to Russia, Ota, met with Foreign Minister Arita on the afternoon of the 19th to report on the domestic situation in Soviet Russia, international relations, and its Far Eastern policy, in considerable detail, and made important recommendations, saying that Soviet Russia is preparing a large army in the Far East, and Japan should strengthen its military strength stationed in Manchuria to confront it. Depending on the attitude of Soviet Russia, a non-aggression treaty or other peaceful measures could be considered. The main points of Ambassador Ota's report are as follows:

(1) Domestic Situation: The Second Five-Year Plan of Soviet Russia has been successful, domestic materials are gradually becoming abundant, and various aspects of industry, mining, and agriculture have been stimulated by the Stakhanovite movement, increasing their production volume. Along with the training of the people, national power is growing day by day. Recently, a new draft constitution was announced, gradually leaning towards capitalism.

(2) International Relations: Soviet Russia once regarded the League of Nations as a base for anti-Russian movements, but since its participation in the League of Nations, Soviet Russia's position in European diplomacy has suddenly become advantageous. It has concluded a mutual assistance treaty with France, and formed friendly relations with Britain and various small countries closely related to France, to strengthen its international position. The development of Soviet Russia's international relations and the changes in domestic affairs are important matters that deserve our attention.

(3) Far Eastern Policy: Soviet Russia has 300,000 troops stationed in the Far East, and its line of fortresses on the border has been completed. There is also the double-tracking of the Siberian Railway, the construction of the BAM Railway, and the construction of new industrial cities. Its work to complete its military preparations in the Far East is proceeding steadily, and its strength far exceeds Japan's military strength. Moreover, Soviet Russia has no intention of accepting Japan's request to withdraw its troops or establish a demilitarized zone. Therefore, Japan must also increase its military strength, with the standard of money in Europe as a diplomatic support. (20th Allied Telegram)

Soviet Representative Criticizes Japanese Policy at the Pacific Conference

Yosemite, California, USA The Pacific Conference continued today. The Soviet representative criticized Japan's foreign policy, saying that the Japanese admit that their foreign policy varies according to the place, which is astounding. Soviet Russia has no other policy than peace and has signed non-aggression agreements with eleven countries, and has also made the same proposal to Japan. Japan's attitude towards communism is rather strange. It must be known that communism is not an export product and can only be manufactured domestically. Soviet Russia has always thought that a war with Japan is difficult to avoid. The contradictions between the two countries have not reached an unbearable point. The real danger to peace lies in the thinking of the Japanese people. Japan's position is stable, so Soviet Russia's relations with Japan focus on trade and does not hope for a communist coup in Japan, and believes that communism and capitalism have great potential for peaceful cooperation. After the Soviet representative finished speaking, the Japanese representative responded that Japan also intends to resolve all disputes without using force, and believes that it is necessary to create new organizations to truly maintain peace. (19th National Telegram)

Japanese Naval and Army Plans, Minister of Finance Will Demand Concessions

(Tokyo) The Navy's budget has always focused on the implementation of the first and second supplementary plans and the improvement of capital ships. However, from next year onwards, it will focus on expanding new military preparations such as building replacement ships, preparing auxiliary ships, and strengthening the air force, and establishing a national defense to deal with the US naval power in 1941. The Navy authorities have implemented two supplementary plans to make up for the inferiority of the naval power to Britain and the United States, and have been carrying out the transformation of capital ships since Showa 10. The three-year plan will be completed in its main part by the end of this year. Therefore, from next year, the final part of the three-year plan will be implemented, such as the transformation of aircraft carriers, auxiliary ships, and other works. From the year after that, the surplus of the budget will be used exclusively to implement new military preparations such as building capital ships and other new warships, and increasing the air force. (20th Allied Telegram)

(Tokyo) The Army authorities plan to save as much as possible in the Army budget for next year in order to enrich national defense, reform general administration, and stabilize the people's lives. Minister of the Army Terauchi discussed the issue of the scope of savings in the Army budget with Major General Umezu, Director of the Military Affairs Bureau Isoya, and Director of the Financial Affairs Bureau Hirate on the afternoon of the 19th. (20th Allied Telegram)

(Tokyo) Minister of Finance Baba has a general understanding of the true intentions of the Army and Navy in determining national policy and national defense plans. Based on this, he has reviewed the revenue plan and has obtained a general draft. Therefore, he visited Prime Minister Hirota on the morning of the 20th to conduct important consultations. The budgets requested by various provinces are as high as 1.5 billion yuan for new requests. If the base budget of 1.6 billion yuan for next year is added, it will reach a total of 3.2 billion yuan, an increase of 900 million yuan compared to this year's budget. Although methods such as increasing taxes and raising funds from special accounts or seeking increased revenue from government industries are used, this request cannot be met. Therefore, in view of the current state of finance, it is necessary to demand considerable concessions from various provinces. In particular, the largest of the new projects is the national defense budget. If this problem cannot be resolved, other national policies cannot be decided. However, the government has long declared its national policy and naturally needs to proceed accordingly. However, even if a national defense-first budget is compiled, it is impossible not to demand considerable concessions from the Army and Navy. This is the unanimous opinion of the Prime Minister and the Minister of Finance. In addition, regarding the national policy items, the Prime Minister and the Minister of Finance exchanged views frankly based on the four major policies, and considerable clues have been obtained. Regarding the national policies that have fallen out, a research committee will be established to study them, so that there will be no loss of face among the cabinet members, etc., in order to seek coordination within the cabinet. It has been decided to follow this policy and hold the second Tianxiang Conference with Minister of the Army Terauchi and Minister of the Navy Nagano around the cabinet meeting on the 21st to conduct important consultations centered on the national defense budget. (20th Allied Telegram)

The Content of Japan's National Policy Items Has Been Decided, Totaling 350 Million Yuan

(Tokyo) Prime Minister Hirota and Minister of Finance Baba met today and, based on the four major policies for deciding national policy, most of the contents of the national policy items, except for two or three remaining items, have been decided as follows:

(1) National Defense Policy: The strengthening of the Army and Navy's national defense should be recognized as a priority.

(2) Reorganization of the Tax System (including tax increases): The central and local governments will uniformly implement fundamental reorganization of the tax system.

(3) Promotion of Industry and Trade: Fuel and raw material national policy, state-owned electricity, promotion of trade, and aviation national policy.

(4) Stabilization of National Life: Extending the length of compulsory education, insurance national policy, reorganization of rural debt, and the local finance transfer system.

In addition, national policies that are being studied include facilities related to arable land issues, disaster relief facilities, civil engineering national policy, immigration national policy, expansion of foreign affairs agencies, and so on. Whether these undecided national policies should be considered national policies or should be considered budgets and requests should be decided after consultation between the Minister of Finance and the minister in charge. In addition, the Ministry of Justice's enrichment fees and the Ministry of Communications' maritime transport national policy will likely be requested as additional budgets for general policies in order to handle them. (20th Allied Telegram)

(Tokyo) The work of deciding national policy has entered the final stage. The total amount of national policies proposed by various provinces is 100 million yuan. After reorganization, it may increase slightly. The total amount of more than 30 items proposed by various provinces at the beginning reached 350 million yuan. After review by the three chief cabinet secretaries, the decision was made to accept or reject them. The civil engineering projects of the Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry and the Ministry of Home Affairs and the judicial national policy were transferred to new requests, or reorganized by reducing expenses and transferring them to the next fiscal year, to 160 million to 170 million yuan. However, after Minister of Finance Baba individually negotiates with various provinces in the future, the total amount of national policy expenses may be further reduced to around 100 million yuan. (20th Allied News Agency Telegram)

If a World War Breaks Out, the US and Canada Will Inevitably Be Involved, the Defense of Canada and Australia Is Important

Toronto, Canada Lord Iliffe, president of the Federation of British Empire Chambers of Commerce, said in a speech to various Canadian and British Empire clubs today that the United States and Canada could not avoid being caught up in the vortex of a world war. Australia, New Zealand, and South Africa have each prepared their own air defenses, so the issue of Canadian air defense is extremely important. Iliffe also said that Toronto, Montreal, Ottawa, and Vancouver in Canada are all within the range of incendiary bombs dropped by aircraft with a range of 5,000 miles. He now believes that Canadians do not have a complete understanding of the dangerous situation of the coastal areas of Canada. (19th Reuters Telegram)

Sydney, Australia Sir Pierre, the Australian Minister for the Army, recently declared here that the Australian government has decided to implement a national defense supplementary plan in the shortest possible time. (20th Havas Telegram)

US Shipbuilding Plan, a Cruiser Suddenly Catches Fire

(Washington) According to this year's shipbuilding program, commercial shipyards will undertake the construction of six 1,500-ton destroyers and three 1,550-ton submarines. The number of ships undertaken by government-run naval shipyards is the same. To date, a total of 79 new ships are under construction, including 12 submarines and 51 destroyers. (20th Havas Telegram)

Quincy, USA The naval cruiser Vincennes, built by the Bethlehem Shipbuilding Corporation, suddenly caught fire in the factory here today. It is said that the fire was caused by a short circuit. It has now been extinguished, with losses of 25,000 yuan. Seven fires have broken out in Bethlehem Company's shipyards since January. In 1934, when the Quincy was under construction, there was also a fire, with losses of 150,000 yuan. Every time a fire breaks out, there are rumors of espionage plots, but no evidence has been found. (19th National Telegram)

Wang Zhengting Will Be Appointed as Ambassador to the United States, the US Has Not Expressed Anything

(Washington) Personnel at the Chinese Embassy here declined to comment on the news from Nanjing that former Foreign Minister Dr. Wang Zhengting would succeed Shi Zhaoji as the Chinese Ambassador to the United States. They only knew that Shi had requested leave from his government and was willing to resign and return to his country. Ambassador Shi is currently vacationing in Bair Schülvenez, and State Department officials are also keeping silent about this news. However, it is heard that Dr. Wang has a very good reputation in Washington and has many friends. He recently traveled to the United States in the capacity of director of the Far East region of the International Rotary Club and is now in Germany. (19th National Telegram)

Soviet Russian Military Court Continues to Hear Anti-Government Case, Defendants Confess to Plotting to Harm Stalin, Trotsky Makes Grand Statements Abroad

(Moscow) The military judge of the Supreme Court of the Soviet Union publicly tried 14 Soviet counter-revolutionaries, including Zinoviev, today. The chairman was Oulirik, and the Soviet state lawyer Vishexinsky served as the prosecutor. All defendants refused lawyer defense. The chairman then declared that the defendants had the right to accept lawyer defense. According to the indictment, all defendants directly admitted their crimes, while Smiloff and Gortchimen denied direct participation in the preparation of this terror, but Sgorgol did not deny participating in the work under the control of Trotsky. (19th TASS Telegram)

(Moscow) Zinoviev, Kamenev, and twelve other reactionary elements, former members of the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Communist Party, were accused of conspiring to use terrorist means to subvert the country and endanger the lives of leaders of the current government, especially the General Secretary of the Communist Party, Stalin, under the instigation of the anti-cadre leader Trotsky. The case opened yesterday and did not adjourn until night. The trial was held overnight. The court was set up in the trade union office. The military police were heavily guarded, and those who entered the court to listen were also strictly investigated in advance to show seriousness. At the opening of the trial yesterday, prosecutor Lingor demanded that the defendants be sentenced to death and declared that the economic source of these terrorists was the financing of certain employees of the National Bank. When carrying out terrorist acts, they were divided into two groups. If the first group failed, the second group would take over. The famous political commentator and editor-in-chief of Pravda, Radek, the executive committee member of the Third International, Pyatakov, the former ambassador to Britain, Sokolnikov, and the important member of the Communist Party, Selebryanov, were all listed in the second group. The current People's Commissar for Transportation, Belaev, knew about the original commission of this conspiracy in 1932. At that time, the defendants looked calm, but Avschkeemov criticized the government's major events when answering questions, and was reprimanded by the court and withdrew silently. (20th Havas Telegram)

(Moscow) The defendant David confessed without reservation to the attempt to assassinate Stalin. The criminals were all related to the murder case of Stalin's adjutant Morov in 1934, and colluded with a part of the German secret reconnaissance to engage in espionage, terrorism, assassination of Stalin and other actions. According to the official news agency, the criminals have all confessed their guilt. When David was questioned, he confessed that in the autumn of 1932, Trotsky asked him to undertake the assassination of Stalin. He had participated in the 7th National Congress of the Communist Party in order to shoot Stalin, but because the seat was too far from the podium, he could not achieve this goal. Another defendant, Walburg, confessed that he entered Russia with a fake passport. The passport was obtained by entrusting a German secret detective clerk in Prague with 100 pounds of British gold. The gold was paid by a certain agency of Trotsky. He met with several important members of the German secret detective department and discussed the first visit to Moscow and the plan to implement terrorist actions. It is heard that this confession has been verified by Walburg's brother, who is also one of the defendants and served as a German secret detective. According to the confession, his brother told him that a certain important member of the German secret detective department said that anyone who participated in terrorist actions in Russia could be protected in Germany. The authorities have investigated and found that a terrorist group was presided over by the defendant Luruy. The terrorist actions of assassinating Stalin and other Soviet Russian leaders were organized by Weiz, a member of the German fascist party and representative of Himmler, the director of the German secret detective department. According to the TASS news agency, the confessions obtained after the opening of the trial today have proved that Trotsky and his sons are guilty of personally directing and organizing terrorist actions that are detrimental to the Soviet Russian leaders. If the Trotsky and his sons can be immediately arrested, they will be tried and convicted by the military court or the Supreme Court.

The defendant Zinoviev confessed everything without any reservation. According to the confession, the most active and strongest advocate of terrorist actions in the case was Smirnov. Zinoviev replied to the questioning that part of his plan was to feign loyalty to the Communist Party while secretly engaging in various terrorist activities. The defendant Lingold confessed that they premeditated to make Noviev and Kamenev visit the Communist Party four times to feign hospitality and gain Stalin's trust. After gaining power, they would exterminate all the terrorist members who could expose their crimes in the positions where they were. Another defendant confessed that a man named Bogdan was ordered to assassinate Stalin. Because Bogdan was slow to carry out this mission, the leader of the party told him that if he could not kill Stalin, he should commit suicide. So Bogdan had no choice but to commit suicide.

When the defendants confessed their crimes, they often quarreled with each other. Kamenev had gray hair and looked dignified. During the interrogation, he admitted that he personally hated Stalin. The fact that the defendants repeatedly tried to carry out terrorist actions was due to Stalin's seizure of power. As for his hatred of Stalin, it was because Stalin's socialist policies were successful. Jia also mentioned a conspiracy that involved many people, including the official spokesman for Soviet Russian foreign affairs, Lighteck, and the journalist of Izvestia, the organ of the All-Russian Executive Committee, Bukharin. (20th Reuters Telegram)

(Moscow) The Soviet Russian authorities arrested another thirteen people today for the Trotsky counter-revolution case, including one woman. They may be tried separately. It will take a week to complete the trial of the sixteen people who are on trial. (20th National Telegram)

Oslo, Norway The anti-cadre leader Trotsky declared to reporters that in a few years, he will turn the Moscow authorities into defendants in order to redress this prison. The reactionary case woven by Moscow this time is purely the result of personal revenge. He will disclose various documents to prove that he is innocent. (20th Havas Telegram)

Fierce Fighting in Northern Spain, Government Forces Make Slight Progress, Order Women and Children to Take Refuge in Preparation for a Decisive Battle, Hundreds of Foreign Volunteers Go to the Front Line

San Sebastian Government army authorities anticipated that the rebels were about to launch a major offensive, and today ordered all women and children to leave the country in preparation for a decisive battle. (20th National Telegram)

Hendaye, France Spanish government forces today forced the rebels in the Irun area of northern Spain to retreat during the fierce fighting, and recovered some territory. Several shells fell on the town of Irun. Irun has iron mines, hot springs, and is famous for its pottery industry. The most important customs of Spain are located in the town, and troops are stationed there in peacetime. (20th Reuters Telegram)

Hendaye, France The most intense war since the beginning of the civil war in northern Spain has broken out. The rebels and government forces are fighting a desperate battle in the north to capture Irun and San Sebastian. A large number of rebels have occupied the mountains overlooking Irun. The two sides are only 200 yards apart and are fighting each other with machine guns and artillery. A thousand militiamen from Bilbao have arrived in Irun to increase the strength of the government forces. It is heard that hundreds of foreign volunteers and some machine gun experts have also arrived in San Sebastian to help the government forces defend the port. At the same time, the number of refugees is increasing day by day. Every day, 500 women and children pass through the border, while the strong men remain behind to help the people's front. There are still many refugees staying on the Spanish border, preparing to leave the country immediately if the war extends to the border. The radio station of the rebels in Seville broadcast news last night, in which there was no news of the war, and asked the public to donate records of the national anthems of Germany, Italy, and Portugal. (20th Reuters Telegram)

Oslo, Norway The anti-cadre leader Trotsky declared to reporters that in a few years, he will turn the Moscow authorities into defendants in order to redress this prison. The reactionary case woven by Moscow this time is purely the result of personal revenge. He will disclose various documents to prove that he is innocent. (20th Havas Telegram)

Spanish Warship Searches German Merchant Ship; German Government Lodges Protest

(Berlin) News that the German ship "Champlain," carrying refugees from Spain en route to Genoa, was detained today seven and a half miles off the coast of Cadiz by a Spanish government cruiser has aroused extreme indignation in Germany. The Spanish warship initially fired three shots at the German ship, forcing it to stop, and then sent sailors from a submarine to board and search the vessel. German officials view this as a serious incident, stating that the Spanish warship's firing upon and stopping the German ship outside its territorial waters violates international law. (Reuters, 20th)

(Berlin) The semi-official German News Agency issued a statement today claiming that the German merchant ship "Cameroon" was sailing from the German coast to Genoa, Italy, when it was ordered to detour to Cadiz, Spain, to pick up German expatriates for evacuation. However, seven and a half miles off the Spanish coast, the Spanish government submarine "Pizi VI" and cruiser "Libertad" blocked its path and sent personnel to board and search the ship. Finally, the ship was ordered to change course and sail towards the Mediterranean. News of this incident has greatly shocked political circles here, who consider it a serious matter not to be underestimated. Semi-official sources believe that, according to international law, warships of any country are not allowed to search merchant ships of other countries outside territorial waters (three miles from shore). The search of the "Cameroon" occurred outside Spanish territorial waters, which is a violation of the principle of freedom of the seas. Such an action is absolutely unjustifiable unless the two countries are at war. The German government should demand from the Madrid government (1) a formal apology and (2) compensation for losses. It is known that the Führer Hitler is currently vacationing at his villa in Berchtesgaden, Bavaria, and he will personally decide how to handle this matter. (Havas, 19th)

(Berlin) Regarding the German merchant ship "Cameroon" being illegally inspected by a Spanish warship outside Spanish territorial waters, the government has instructed its chargé d'affaires in Spain to lodge a strong protest with the Spanish government. Simultaneously, German warships have been ordered to protect German ships outside Spanish territorial waters to prevent further illegal inspections by Spanish warships. (Havas, 20th)

(Berlin) Regarding the "Cameroon" incident, semi-official sources have stated that the ship belongs to the "Ullman" shipping company and intended to detour to Cadiz, Spain, en route to Italy, and was not carrying any military supplies. (Havas, 20th)

(London) London legal circles strongly disagree with the German official claim that the Spanish government cruiser's inspection of the German ship "Champlain" violates international law. International law experts insist that, although the two sides in the Spanish Civil War have not been legally recognized as belligerents, they have been recognized as such in fact. Therefore, both sides have the right to inspect ships of other countries. (Reuters, 20th)

Spanish Government Announces Blockade of Territorial Waters; Britain Demands Clear Explanation

(London) Britain has requested the Spanish government to provide a clear explanation of its intention to declare a blockade. The Spanish government recently issued an order declaring certain areas of Spanish territorial waters blockaded, and subsequently issued a second order, prompting the British authorities to demand a clear definition. As of now, the British government has not recognized the Spanish blockade. (Reuters, 20th)

Britain Takes the Lead in Implementing; Franco-Italian Talks Continue

(London) The Department of Trade today canceled all previously issued export licenses for various weapons, ammunition, and aircraft destined for mainland Spain, Spanish territories, and Spanish Morocco. This is further proof of Britain's strict adherence to neutrality in the Spanish Civil War. The cancellation was announced by order of the Department of Trade, and henceforth the export of all kinds of weapons, ammunition, and aircraft to Spain is completely prohibited, with a detailed list of over two hundred prohibited weapons and ammunition items attached. The last item on the list is "aircraft, whether assembled or unassembled, and aircraft engines," thus including all types of aircraft, both military and civilian, within this ban, regardless of whether they are transported by ship or by their own power. Violators of this ban who continue to sell aircraft to Spain will be severely punished. This stringent measure by Britain is in line with the British government's repeated declarations of upholding the principle of non-intervention in the Spanish Civil War, and is implemented early, before an agreement can be reached by the various countries regarding the French proposal. This action by Britain serves two main purposes: firstly, it reflects a deep fear that the principles of non-intervention, if not implemented soon, will lead to various dangers; secondly, it expresses the hope that the governments of the related countries will reach an agreement quickly. (Reuters, 19th)

(London) The Department of Trade has issued an order stipulating that, from today onwards, no export licenses will be issued for the transport of any kind of ordnance, bullets, explosives, or commercial or military aircraft to Spain and Spanish territories. According to well-informed sources, when the British and French governments reached an agreement on non-intervention in the Spanish Civil War, they exchanged notes stating that the agreement would only take effect after the governments of the relevant countries agreed to participate, but did not stipulate that Britain had an obligation to implement an embargo. Therefore, today's ban is a unilateral initiative by the British government in the area of non-intervention policy. Domestically, although Parliament passed a law in 1931 restricting the export of ammunition, it does not apply to other items, and the government has no legal right to restrict the export of aircraft. Therefore, the measures taken by the Department of Trade today are bold and innovative, intended to set an example for Germany and Italy to follow. Furthermore, the French government previously stated that if the Italian government did not provide a satisfactory response to the non-intervention proposal, France would resume freedom of action. If this materializes, the British government seems determined to adopt a strict neutral stance, and the ban issued by the Department of Trade today represents this stance in technical terms. It is said that the non-intervention agreement previously reached between Britain and France will not have mandatory force until it is jointly accepted by the countries concerned. The ban is purely an initiative by the British government, aimed at assisting the efforts of the French government. (Havas, 19th)

(London) After the Department of Trade issued an order yesterday prohibiting the transport of munitions and aircraft to mainland Spain and its territories, the government, to prevent aviation personnel from falsely reporting their whereabouts and intentionally undermining this law, has decided to authorize the Secretary of State for Air to revoke the pilot's licenses of any aviation personnel who disregard the law. The Department has also decided to warn all pilots throughout the country not to violate the law. (Havas, 20th)

Portsmouth: Two employees of a British airline attempted to fly an aircraft to Madrid today to join the government forces, but crashed shortly after takeoff due to a lack of flight experience, sustaining serious injuries. (National Telegram, 20th)

(London) Representatives of the Labour Party and trade unions visited Foreign Secretary Eden this afternoon to discuss the situation in Spain. The nature of the talks has not been disclosed, but the visit may be related to the Labour Party's and Liberal Party's efforts to convene Parliament as soon as possible. Acting Leader of the Opposition, Greenwood, Labour Party Secretary Middleton, and Trade Union Congress Secretary-General Citrine were among the delegation. (Reuters, 20th)

(London) Speaking in Crowe today, First Lord of the Admiralty Hoare addressed the Spanish situation, saying, "We are currently strengthening our national defense to prevent a world war. If our plan can be fully implemented on time, our determination will surely succeed." The First Lord of the Admiralty continued that the government has no intention of interfering in the internal affairs of Spain, before detailing the evacuation of foreigners from the Spanish war zone by British ships, stating that British ships provide assistance to British and foreign nationals alike, regardless of their background, and have so far transported 3,500 men, women, and children, of whom 2,000 are British. (Reuters, 19th)

Crowe, Britain: First Lord of the Admiralty Hoare delivered a political speech here today, explaining the importance of Britain maintaining neutrality in the Spanish Civil War, saying that reckless interference could trigger a European war, and denounced former Labour Party leader Lansbury's proposal that the British government force the Spanish government and rebel forces to cease hostilities, saying that politics had become so corrupt that the two parties were killing each other, replacing voting with guns and bombs, and that such civil wars, assassinations, and violent deaths would inevitably lead to the disintegration of major powers. (National Telegram, 19th)

(London) Sir Samuel Hoare, the First Lord of the Admiralty, delivered a speech near Croydon Park, sharply attacking the opposition Labour Party and clearly stating that the British government is eager to maintain neutrality in the Spanish Civil War, saying, "Our people all cherish peace, but we oppose the Labour Party. They are nominally leftists, but in reality, they are warmongers, talking about war without considering whether the naval, land, and air forces are sufficient, as if they could fight without them. Such absurdity is evident. If we were to force one of the warring parties in Spain to accept our will, the impact would engulf all European countries, which must be approached with caution." (Havas, 19th)

(Rome) The Italian reply to the French proposal for neutrality in the Spanish Civil War was delivered today by Foreign Minister Count Ciano to the French Ambassador Jean Blondel. Ciano declined to disclose the contents of the reply, but said that talks on the issue of neutrality would continue. Meanwhile, a spokesman for the Propaganda Ministry said that if the revolutionary government organized by General Franco and others in Spain could control the entire country, Italy would naturally recognize it, but that now was not the time to discuss the issue of recognition. According to reliable sources, Italian Prime Minister Mussolini believes that Italian involvement in the current situation in Spain would trigger a European war, and that once the warring countries are exhausted, communism could take the opportunity to rise. Therefore, senior officials, army commanders, and diplomats generally believe that Mussolini will do his best to avoid international disputes, while also acknowledging that Italy has been secretly assisting the rebel forces. Count Ciano dismissed as completely unfounded reports that he was preparing to intervene in Spanish affairs, but said that Italy has a million-strong army, so the general view is that if anything happens, Italy will be able to act immediately. It is reported that a squadron of Italian warships has arrived in the Bay of Gaeta between Naples and Rome, not far from a naval exercise area. Observers believe that this may be related to the current situation in Spain. (National Telegram, 19th)

(Rome) The Italian government previously made two reservations regarding the French proposal for a non-intervention agreement in the Spanish Civil War: (1) prohibiting all countries from providing financial assistance to the two warring factions in Spain, and (2) prohibiting citizens of all countries from voluntarily joining the warring factions in Spain. Subsequently, France replied with a polite refusal, and Italy's second answer has not yet been submitted. French Ambassador Blondel met with Foreign Minister Count Ciano today to discuss Italy's reservations at length, but no conclusion was reached and the meeting ended. It is reported that Italy considers France's previous answer to be lacking in clarity, and is now waiting for France to provide further clarification. (Havas, 19th)

Situation of Spanish Government Troops Defending

Spanish Militias Departing for the Front

Inspection of the Two Armies' Positions

Hendaye, France: The Spanish Northern Front is now focused on the area of San Sebastián and Irún. This correspondent traveled this morning to inspect the road between Irún and Barcelona. The two armies' front lines are less than 500 meters apart. The rebel outpost has now advanced to the Aranda farm. The residents there have all fled into French territory. The surrounding mountain peaks are all occupied by rebel troops. When this correspondent arrived at the area, he saw forty supply trucks transporting military supplies to the mountaintop, and an armored vehicle with red and yellow flags transporting troops across the Szterecha bridge. The bridge was previously destroyed by the government forces and has now been rebuilt by the rebel forces. The government forces' outpost is in the Dapença area. Sentries are either hidden behind sandbags or stationed atop high mountains, watching the rebel forces. A section of the road that crosses between the two armies has been destroyed by government forces and has many landmines planted, but there has been no fighting along the entire front line until noon. Both sides are optimistic about the future. (Havas, 20th)

Barcelona: Implementing a New Economic System

Barcelona: The Economic Committee of the Autonomous Region of Catalonia, composed of representatives from various parties in the Popular Front and representatives from various trade unions, has resolved to implement a new economic system immediately. The content is as follows:

(1) The quantity of production in the province should be balanced with the needs of consumers. All non-essential factories should immediately cease production.

(2) Foreign trade should be exclusively operated by the provincial government so that the new economic system is not affected by external shocks.

(3) The land in the province should be divided into large, medium, and small categories. Large-sized land should be collectivized immediately and cultivated by the trade unions of the province. The crops produced from medium and small-sized land should be sold and purchased by the trade unions.

(4) Various large-scale industries, public utilities, and public transport should also be collectivized.

(5) Financial affairs should be managed by the working class.

(6) Industries that continue to be managed by private individuals should be managed by trade unions.

(7) Farms and factories should increase the price of agricultural products in order to absorb a large number of unemployed workers, and urban workers should be encouraged to return to agriculture as much as possible.

(8) Eliminate exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies, and replace them with a simple tax system. (Havas, 19th)

Spanish Civil War Claims 50,000 Lives; Leaving Behind 70,000 Orphans and Widows

Lisbon: According to recent estimates from various sources, 50,000 people have died since the outbreak of the Spanish rebellion. In the major battles at the end of last week, 2,000 people died in Badajoz, 1,000 in Manresa, and more than 1,000 in the province of Teruel. (National Telegram, 19th)

(Paris) L'Excelsior recently published a report from its correspondent in Madrid stating that the number of deaths in Spain since the outbreak of the civil war is estimated at 25,000 on the government side and 30,000 on the rebel side. Three thousand militiamen were executed by the rebel forces in the cities of Badajoz and Mérida, and this number is included in the above figures. Furthermore, according to refugees who escaped from the province of Teruel, more than 1,000 militiamen in the province were executed by the rebel army. In addition, many civilians were also massacred, leaving behind 25,000 widows and 60,000 orphans. (Havas, 19th)

Czech President's Speech: Not Worried About German Aggression; Czech-German Relations Move With France and Germany

Prague, Czech Republic: President Beneš recently traveled to North Bohemia and stayed overnight in Zeleny Brod yesterday, where he delivered a speech, saying, "Some say that Germany will inevitably invade our country in the future. In my opinion, this is absurd. It should be known that our country has a population of fifteen million, is located in the center of Europe, and if any country wants to endanger our existence, it will inevitably cause a European crisis, which no one wants to see. Moreover, our country's policy towards European countries will never hinder the relationship between Czechoslovakia and Germany, preventing them from obtaining a concrete resolution. The five countries that signed the Locarno Pact will hold a meeting this fall. All obstacles that hinder European peace will be cleared at that time." President Beneš then reiterated that Czechoslovakia's foreign policy moves with four factors in Europe: the attitudes of Poland, Italy, Germany, and Soviet Russia. "There are many absurd and untrue reports about the relationship between Czechoslovakia and Soviet Russia. These are all fabrications and have ulterior motives. In short, the most important issue at present is the relationship between Czechoslovakia and Germany, and the mutual understanding between France and Germany is also related to the survival of Czechoslovakia. If these two countries can reach a compromise, then some of the difficult problems between Germany and Czechoslovakia will be automatically eliminated." (Havas, 20th)

(Central News Agency, 20th)

(Changsha) Central Commissioners for the National Election, Zhang Jianbai and others, arrived in Hunan on the 20th. (Special Dispatch, 20th)

(Nanjing) Journalists from various newspapers and news agencies in Nanjing jointly declared that there is no legal organization in the Nanjing press, and only two or three provinces across the country have established journalists' organizations. Most major cities have failed to establish them, which is contrary to the provisions of the Election Law. The majority of journalists in the country will not be able to participate in this election. Therefore, more than 220 journalists from various newspapers and news agencies jointly issued a declaration on the 20th, echoing the proposal of the Wuhan Journalists' Association, and elaborating on it in detail, requesting the Central Government and the General Election Headquarters to find a way to remedy the situation, and also requesting colleagues from all over the country to agree with the declaration. The full text of the declaration is as follows: This time, our Party, in accordance with the will of the late Premier, is convening a National Congress, promoting the principles of the Three People's Principles, and permanently establishing the foundation of the nation. Billions of people are encouraged, and the world is delighted. According to the provisions of the table attached to the National Congress Representative Election Law, news reporter organizations elect 11 representatives to contribute their opinions on national affairs as much as possible. This proves the Central Government's emphasis on public opinion. All colleagues are grateful. However, Article 19 of the Election Law stipulates, "The professional organizations and free professional organizations participating in the election are limited to those established in accordance with the law before the promulgation of this law." The development of the news industry in China has been late, and the qualifications of reporters engaged in the news industry still lack legal standards. The complexity of the internal situation is the same as that of those engaged in the news industry. At present, the organizations of journalists in various provinces across the country are less than two or three provinces. Even in major cities, they have not been fully established. Nanjing is the capital of the country, and the news industry has developed rapidly in the past decade. In any aspect, its importance in the domestic news industry cannot be denied. However, as the legal organization mentioned in the Election Law, it is still missing. In this National Congress' election of free professionals, as stipulated in the Election Law, the majority of journalists in the country will not be able to participate in this election. If we allow the journalists' organizations in a few places with rudimentary organizations to monopolize the matter, it will not be enough to represent the will of the national news industry, and it will not be what the journalists in those three or four places want to do. This fact was previously resolved and telegraphed by the Wuhan Journalists' Association, and we are further elaborating on its meaning and appealing after it. The law cannot ignore the facts. If the law is applied to the facts, it will sometimes be exhausted, and we can only change the law to remedy its exhaustion. This is the general rule of relief in the laws of various countries. Now, the situation of the news industry in our country is like this, the qualifications of reporters themselves are confused, and the organizations of journalists are so incomplete. It is extravagant to force the election of representatives. It is neither what the news industry wants to hear, nor is it the original intention of the central government's legislation. We are loyal to the Three People's Principles and deeply support the National Congress. However, we cannot but list the reasons for the difficulties in the election methods, and request the Central Government and the General Election Headquarters to find a way to remedy the situation. All our colleagues, regardless of distance, will express their support for this matter. We jointly appeal, and everyone has a responsibility. We respectfully submit this true statement for your clear judgment. (Central News Agency, 20th)

Statistics on the Number of Farmers Nationwide

(Nanjing) China's total population is said to be over 400 million, but there are no precise statistics on whether it has increased or decreased in recent years. The Statistics Department of the Ministry of Interior has been conducting a survey of the national population, and materials from various provinces have been collected for the most part. They are currently being organized and the statistical results will soon be made public. Farmers account for the largest proportion of the national population, accounting for more than 80% of the total population. Therefore, farmers occupy an absolute majority position in China. The Statistics Department of the Ministry of Interior has already obtained the results of the survey on the number of farmers and the proportion of various types of tenant farmers. The total number of farmers nationwide is 320,384,018. Regarding the proportion of tenant farmers, there are no results for the five provinces of Xinjiang, Ningxia, Mongolia, and Tibet. In the remaining 25 provinces, owner-cultivators account for 23%, and tenant farmers account for 32%. The number of farmers in each region is as follows: Yellow River region: 102,766,402; Yangtze River region: 118,902,974; Pearl River region: 24,039,435; Fujian-Zhejiang region: 22,378,928; Northeast region: 21,004,590; Northwest region: 6,641,265; Rehe-Chahar region: 4,742,606; Yunnan-Guizhou region: 12,051,618; Mongolia-Tibet region: 6,856,200. (20th, Central News Agency dispatch)

International Commercial Telegraph August 20 Reuters Special Business Report

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Today is 138 shillings and 2.5 pence, up 0.5 pence.

London Bar Silver: Today, both spot and futures prices on the silver market fell by 0.25 to 19.125 pence. India and speculators sold, but there were no buyers. After the price fell, the market stabilized.

Mountrie Large Spread: The silver market opened this morning, driven by sympathy for the London market. The 12-month forward price was 52 pounds lower than yesterday's market price, at 43.90-44.40.

Exchange Rate

London: The foreign exchange market was slightly mixed this morning. The opening exchange rate between the British pound and the US dollar was 5.033125, down 0.03125 from yesterday's closing rate between the US dollar and the British pound. It rose 0.125 within an hour to 5.034375, but fell 0.125 again at 1:00 PM to 5.033125.

Securities

New York: The stock market fluctuated during the first hour of today, with prices rising slightly. However, they turned downward due to speculative pressure. The volume of transactions was small, and trading was very slow. At noon, most stock prices were slightly lower than yesterday's closing prices. Here are the New York stocks.

Liverpool Wheat: The market opened quietly due to disappointing overnight US telegraphs. Reports of a good harvest in Argentina also prompted retail selling. The market was slow to advance due to a lack of new excitement. At 1:00 PM, the October futures price was 7 shillings and 6 pence, down 0.625 from yesterday's closing price.

New York Cotton: The cotton market opened steadily today due to purchases by the same industry. Later, it loosened slightly due to sympathy for Liverpool and the impact of negative weather news. Before noon, the October futures price was 11.52, down 6 points from yesterday's closing price.

Chicago Wheat: The wheat market was sluggish and uninspired this morning due to a lack of any exciting factors. It opened lower due to profit-taking. The market stabilized after the price fell. At noon, the September futures price was 113.75, down 0.625 from yesterday's closing price. The feed grain market also fell due to profit-taking. At noon, the September futures price fell a net of 1 point from yesterday's closing price to 115.50.
