*Shenbao* Literary Supplement

Bank Stall, Mobil Oil Settles, Foreign Exchange Remains Steady

Yesterday's foreign exchange market saw banks stall, but Mobil Oil aggressively settled, resulting in a stable market. Early morning overseas reports indicated that London's broad terms, both near and far, contracted by 0.0625. New York's silver market remained unchanged. Deferred silver prices in Montreal contracted by 1.1 to 2.2 points. London's raw gold fell by 2 pence. The British pound rose against the US dollar by half a point, the US dollar rose against the British pound by 1.5625, the British pound rose against the French franc by 9 points, and the US dollar fell against the French franc by 0.1875. The Central Bank's official rates were announced, with the British pound and the US dollar remaining unchanged. Customs gold units contracted by 0.3 points. The foreign exchange market opened in the morning with near-term asking prices of 1 shilling 2.375 and 2.4375 pence for the British pound, and 30.1875 yuan for the US dollar. Compared to the previous close, the British pound was slightly looser, while the US dollar was stable. After opening, Chinese merchants slightly stalled. The Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation announced official rates, with the British pound and the US dollar remaining stable and firm. Later, the silver equalization tax was announced, contracting by half a point. However, due to Mobil Oil's aggressive settlement of near and far-term US dollars, the process became slightly tighter. Afterwards, banks slightly conducted swap transactions. Although Mobil Oil continued to aggressively settle, banks seized the opportunity to stall at high prices, resulting in a flat market at noon. In the afternoon, banks slightly stalled in the near term, and the US dollar was also slightly involved in exchange transactions, remaining stable. The initial Indian silver quote was a small 6.5 anna, which did not move in the second quote, and the overall trend remained stable. At closing, the near-term asking prices were 1 shilling 2.375 and 2.40625 pence for the British pound, and 30.1875 yuan for the US dollar. Compared to the previous close, both the near and far-term rates for the British pound and the US dollar were stable. Although banks stalled, Mobil Oil strongly settled US dollars. The transaction records for today will be listed below.

The British pound opened in the morning with near-term asking prices of 1 shilling 2.375 and 2.4375 pence. HSBC stalled December at 3.125 pence. The Orient sold to Korea the same month at the same price. The noon close had near-term asking prices of 1 shilling 2.375 and 2.40625 pence. The after-market lacked transactions. The closing asking prices for spot and August were both 1 shilling 2.375 and 2.40625 pence. September was 2.375 pence, October was 2.34375 and 2.375 pence, November was 2.2125 and 2.34375 pence. Bidding prices were moderately increased.

The US dollar opened in the morning with a near-term asking price of 30.175 yuan. Mobil Oil settled August at 0.1875, September at 0.125, October at 0.0625, November at 30 yuan, December at 29.9375 yuan, and January at 0.875 yuan. China Banking Corporation stalled. China Banking Corporation settled September at 0.125. Macgarry settled August at 0.875, and stalled November at 30 yuan. It also sold to Mobil Oil September at 0.125, October at 0.0625, and November at 30 yuan. The noon close had a near-term asking price of 30.1875 yuan. In the after-market, China Banking Corporation stalled September 5th at 0.1875, and August at the same price. Zhejiang sold to Citibank September at 0.1875. The closing asking prices for spot and August were both 30.1875 yuan. September was 0.125, October was 0.0625, and November was 30 yuan. Bidding prices were increased by 0.025.

The exchange rate between the British pound and the US dollar yesterday saw Macgarry swap out September at 5.0325 yuan.

The exchange rate between the US dollar and the Japanese yen yesterday saw the Central Bank swap to Mitsui at 29.48 yuan.

Securities and Public Bonds: The After-Market Suddenly Sees a Rise

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange experienced significant market fluctuations, with rapid rises and falls. It initially fell due to the Guangxi government reorganization, but later rose due to rumors of new developments in finance. Whether the Guangxi situation can be peacefully resolved has little connection with the market, and the Suiyuan incident also temporarily does not dare to have any changes. Therefore, although the market price slightly fell, any slight good news caused a rapid rebound. The trend is still that rises are easier than falls, and the settlement is becoming increasingly tight, so the future may still have squeezes. Yesterday's events saw morning and evening market conditions that were completely opposite. In the morning opening, selling pressure was extremely strong, but buying interest remained strong. Numbers 10, 16, 26, 35, and 47, etc., were heavily sold, and the market price trended down by 0.3 to 0.4 yuan. Bank C was firm due to Number 77's buying, down only 0.05 yuan. The secondary and afternoon openings were both in swap trades between the long and short sides, with the market price fluctuating between 0.05 and 0.12 yuan, with highs and lows alternating. In the evening market, rumors spread that there were developments in finance, and buyers suddenly rose, with the upward trend becoming swift and fierce, becoming more intense later on. Number 32 first took the lead in buying, and the market sentiment was boosted. Numbers 6, 11, and 35 then followed, and the market temporarily saw a tight rise, with a maximum rise of 0.65 yuan. However, Number 11 sold a large amount of Type A, and the upward trend was slightly frustrated, but it was still good by 0.55 yuan. The trend seems to have a short squeeze possible. As a result, only the current month of Type E and D were down a small 0.25 yuan, while the rest all turned up by 0.05 to 0.67 yuan. The total transaction volume was 11,182,500 yuan. The resulting gains and losses are compared in the table on the left (unit: yuan, transaction sheet unit: 100 yuan).

Cotton Yarn, Cotton Seedlings Growing Well, Spot Cotton Increasingly Soft, This Month's Old Cotton Falls Another 0.75 Yuan

The cotton market is softening, with US cotton falling and Indian cotton also lackluster. New domestic cotton is about to enter the market, the climate is good, which is conducive to cotton seedling growth, people's hearts are increasingly frustrated, especially those who have inventory, and the market price is falling step by step.

New Cotton Approaching the 40 Yuan Mark

At the opening of the spot cotton market, US cotton continued to fall by 12 to 18 points, and Indian cotton was dark and dull. Each month fell by 0.2 to 0.25 yuan. However, after entering the market, due to the yarn market improving and prices approaching the 40 yuan mark, the short side also acted cautiously, and the hovering power was extremely large. The market sentiment was stable, and it slowly recovered. However, the current weather is favorable, which is conducive to agricultural production and growth. According to various news sources, cotton production is thriving, and there is no lack of sellers during rises. At the close, it was again sluggish, and as a result, each month fell by 0.15 yuan compared to the previous day's close, and August fell by 0.5 yuan. The afternoon opening saw continued exhaustion and weakness in the market trend, and buyers were scarce. As a result, May fell by another 0.05 to 0.1 yuan compared to the morning close, and August fell by 0.45 yuan alone. The following sources of capital: Yu Kang 1,100 bales, Yuan Da 1,300 bales, Geng Feng 3,400 bales, Yong Yu 1,800 bales, Yi Cheng 6,900 bales, Zhen Da 1,300 bales, He Xing 1,300 bales, Xin Cheng 1,200 bales, Tong Ji bought 1,800 bales, Ju Xing 3,200 bales, Sen Kang 1,800 bales, Ren Feng 3,100 bales, Tai Chang 1,700 bales, Chang Feng 2,000 bales, Yuan Yi 2,000 bales, and Xin Chang 1,200 bales. Cotton Still Not Open for Trading

The current cotton consumption is mediocre, factories are sluggish, and there is no source, it is said.

Yarn Market Continues to Decline

The yarn market continues to decline, with a sluggish trend. This is because the overseas yarn and cotton conditions are moving downstream, people's hearts are empty, and at the same time, current yarn sales are less. However, Sichuanese merchants are still doing well, while other merchants are buying even less. In fact, new cotton is gradually entering the market, and the short side is becoming bolder. However, the inventory of yarn is thinner than before, it is said.

Spot Yarn Falls Another Yuan Weak

At the opening of the spot yarn market, Grade 3 US cotton yarn and cotton continued to fall, and the market sentiment softened. However, new sellers were not seen to be very enthusiastic, and the market was soft and hard. Each month only fell by 0.7 to 0.8 yuan. After the second session, it was heard that Sichuan merchants were eagerly buying in for this yarn, and Dafu heavily covered shorts, and the market price slowly rebounded. However, Geng Feng's long side slightly closed out, and the market situation was peaceful. As a result, each month fell by 0.25 yuan compared to the previous day's close, and September and October rose by 0.1 to 0.2 yuan. The afternoon opening saw a flat and weak market situation, and trading was not smooth in the market. The sentiment was scattered, and it was generally impossible to get rid of the hovering situation. It was heard that a portion of the yarn from Sichuan merchants had not been negotiated and had not been traded, and the market sentiment was sluggish. As a result, each month fell by another 0.2, 0.4, 0.5, and 0.8 yuan compared to the morning close. The First National Cotton Production Estimate Announced Yesterday

The China Cotton Industry Statistics Association announced the first national cotton production estimate for 1936 at 5:00 PM on August 20, 1936, as follows: Cotton field area 338,172,310 ares (equivalent to 55,041,066 old system mu)

Raw cotton production 9,606,396 quintals (equivalent to 16,379,194 old system dan)

This estimate: (1) is based on reports compiled from twelve provinces including Hebei, Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, Shaanxi, Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, Anhui, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Sichuan, and two cities, Shanghai and Tianjin; (2) is based on the cotton crop conditions before August 15; (3) the losses caused by disasters to the cotton crop in various provinces before August 15 have been included in the calculation; (4) the "old system mu" of cotton fields is 60 square zhang per mu, and the "old system dan" of cotton production is 100 jin per dan.

The historical cotton field production and the estimated numbers of each year in the past five years are compared below (in the table and in the text, those not marked "ares" and "quintals" are "old system mu" and "old system dan").

US Cotton Closing Market Weak

Yesterday, the US cotton opening market was sluggish, still awaiting developments in Europe. Early morning traders and local merchants bought in, and a negative report came out. The market price rose, but then the public sold, and the long side painfully closed out. The western situation was uncertain, and the south and central Texas were reported to have rain. The market price fell. It now needs to be calm, and factories have slightly traded. At the close, the market suddenly softened, with spot falling 18 points and futures falling 13 and 14 points. British cotton spot fell 10 points and futures fell 3 points. Indian cotton initially rose due to a few speculators buying in, but then fell due to showers in Karachi, with Ping Gu Er falling 0.75 rupees, Omla not moving, and Bai Luo Creek falling 1.25 rupees. By the Banks of the Kuntulun River

— Ba

The fiery red sun rose from the eastern horizon, the wind departed from the grasslands, and the distant mountains gradually emerged from the thick morning mist. The Kuntulun River flowed silently, the dense leaves of the poplar trees on its banks gleaming under the sunlight, shimmering and twinkling with the gentle breeze, like still water on a calm lake. Beyond the poplar forest lay a lush expanse of slender reeds, dividing the boundless desert. Yellow sand interspersed with green belts, a brilliant and dotted landscape, like a natural painting, how intoxicating a wilderness! Especially the gurgling water of the Kuntulun River, as if someone were playing music.

At night, my elder brother caught a chill, waking up with a hacking cough. Xikui hastily rummaged through his leather bag for "aspirin," but my brother stopped him:

——Don't bother, I won't get sick. Let the camel driver pack the luggage; let's go stroll along the river, stroll through the woods.

The four of us, hand in hand, walked through the thickets, singing mountain songs from our hometowns, running and jumping into the poplar forest. I plucked some unknown wildflowers and held them in my hands. Little Fan grabbed a branch, pulling himself closer and then letting go, until he finally fell on the grass, and we all burst into laughter.

Just a few steps out of the woods was the Kuntulun River. We walked upstream along the riverbank, chatting and laughing. Suddenly, a gazelle (note) ran across the beach. Xikui quickly shouldered his rifle and aimed, but after the shot rang out, the gazelle had already changed direction and run off. My brother scolded Xikui for wasting a shot. As he spoke, a Mongolian man on horseback galloped towards us from behind, wearing a sheepskin robe, his long braid hitting his back. The sunlight shone upon him, and his robe was greasy and gleaming, as if it had been painted. He carried a large bird gun in his hand, and three gazelles were tied to the horse's back. He stopped in front of us, and spoke to us, in very beautiful Mandarin!

Little Fan seized the opportunity again, asking him all sorts of questions. I didn't pay attention to what they were saying, but carefully observed the hunter's attire. He wore gray felt socks inside his leather boots, making his feet look very clumsy. His belt was adorned with a tobacco pouch, a fire striker, a small knife, a cow horn, and many other odds and ends. As we were talking, another gazelle ran by. The hunter raised his gun, and with a "bang," the gazelle fell with a cry. He immediately opened the cow horn and loaded the gun with gunpowder before running to pick up the gazelle.

My brother thought it was very amusing when he heard the Mongolian hunter ask, "Has Wu Peifu taken office yet!" Filled with curiosity, he wanted to talk to him for a while longer, but the camel driver was calling, saying it was getting late, and we quickly ran back. The camel driver had already packed up the tents and luggage. So, we mounted the camels and set off along the riverbank.

After passing through a stretch of desert, a dense forest appeared to the west, beyond which was an endless expanse of green grassland. After walking for a while, we saw the herds of the ancient girls grazing on the grassland, such a large group! There were camels, horses, and sheep. Young girls were tying red wildflowers to the sheep's horns. The sheep jumped and bleated. The shepherds, drowsy from the sheep's light, lay on the grass, dreaming sweet dreams.

Around noon, we found a Mongolian yurt in a dense thicket. We decided to stop here for a quick meal. When we got off the camels, our legs were so numb that we couldn't stand. We moved around for a while before we could walk freely. So, we ordered the camel driver to set up the stove and cook. We took the opportunity to go see the yurt.

We were all filled with curiosity and a sense of adventure, and walked towards the yurt without hesitation. From afar, a black dog barked and ran towards us. I was so frightened that I hid behind my brother. Before I knew it, a woman came running out of the yurt, stopped the dog, and smiled happily as she invited us into the yurt. A man was squatting on the ground, looking somewhat like a Han Chinese, skinning a rabbit. He immediately dropped what he was doing and came to greet us. The woman brought hot milk tea, her eyes constantly sizing up the guests.

We all sat on the left side of the Buddha statue, while the man held the child and sat at the lower seat. The man sat on the lower seat on the right side, with a pipe in his mouth. Although there was a felt window at the top of the yurt, the air and light felt insufficient, and there was a peculiar smoky odor inside. I took long, slow breaths and talked with the man for a while, learning that he was a Han Chinese from Yulin County, Shaanxi, and coincidentally from our hometown.

Judging by his expression, he seemed to miss his hometown. He asked many questions, making his memories of home even more beautiful and endearing. As he talked about his experiences in the Ejina Banner, a five- or six-year-old child ran in from the felt door and, seeing these unfamiliar strangers, jumped into his mother's arms in surprise, his eyes fixed on us.

——If it weren't for my wife and children, I would have gone home long ago!

When asked about the route to Outer Mongolia, he explained in great detail, telling us how long it would take to get from here to Suoguo, where to find wells, and all the way to Shalen Kuduk and Xila Usu. After drinking our fill of tea, we said goodbye, and he stopped at the door.

As soon as we stepped into the reeds, we ran into a lama:

—Where are you going?

—To Outer Mongolia!

—I'm afraid it won't be easy. The Kherlen area has long forbidden outsiders from passing through!

Unexpectedly, this lama spoke such fluent Mandarin. After asking him carefully, we learned that he was from Rehe and had been to Kulun. We walked through the reeds and looked back at him, and he had already entered the Mongolian yurt we had just visited.

The camel driver was sweating profusely and was a little angry, muttering:

—If you leave me alone to cook again, I'm quitting! I have to fetch water, start the fire, and take care of the camels. How can I manage?

The sky and the earth were vast. Stretched out on the camel's back to look at the incessant stream, grass insects were knocking on the wings, coming and going in the grass on both shores. Camel hooves walked on the hard sand. The sun gradually set to the west, through the sand forest, in front and a prairie appeared, the dusk retreating light, the camels cried, and we began to search for the location with water, couldn't find one, so there was no way but to go forward, slowly heard the dog barking, there must be people nearby, that's how we were relieved.

We found a Mongolian encampment and went in. A couple were already asleep, and five or six lamas were sitting around the stove talking. We asked them where we could find water. A young lama led me to a patch of green grass, where there was a small well, so that we could start cooking. By the time the camel driver had set up the tent, a strong wind had swept in from the desert again.

Note: The gazelle is a type of wild goat found in the desert.

Mourning

— Zang Kejia

This is the second time I've picked up my pen to commemorate a student.

Since coming here to teach, one thing has pleased me, and that is that several students have exceeded my expectations in their literary achievements. I often thought to myself: if they are nurtured properly, I will surely see these elites blossom and bear fruit in the future. Who knew that human hope often only flashes briefly before turning into utter darkness.

Last year, after the student with the surname Hou died of meningitis, not only was I personally grieved, but every student in his entire grade shed tears, especially Xian Si, who shared the same interests. At that time, we selected and printed one of Hou's usual writing assignments, and I added a eulogistic note at the end, which was distributed to all the students in the school as a memento. Anyone who read this piece of writing couldn't help but exclaim, "What a pity for such a genius! Why doesn't heaven let us fools die instead!" Later, in the composition class, I gave the topic of commemorating Hou, and as a result, I received a whole batch of excellent papers, each one written with tears and ink. I, too, drew circle after circle on them, with tears scalding my face. I remember that Xian Si's essay was especially heart-wrenching; his writing was already somewhat sentimental, and such a fitting topic naturally allowed him to blossom flowers of sorrow in the pale ink.

Who would believe that, on the same textbook, under the same topic, students would now have to write essays to commemorate him?

Yes, who would believe it? Even as I write this commemorative text in front of the small lamp, it seems as if he is not really gone forever, never to return to this world, never to return to this small lamp to recite his poems to me.

"Chen Xiansi's poetry is sure to achieve great success!"

I often spread this phrase everywhere with my trumpet-like mouth, spreading it to all the students in the school, spreading it to my friends, wishing I could spread it so that everyone in the world would know about this genius, and only then would I be happy. This was a bit of an impulsive feeling that made me do this. Sure enough, this publicity worked, and no one in the entire school was unaware of this poet. Whether his classmates were joking with him or talking to him seriously, they would all call him "poet," and the word "poet" simply became a proper noun that existed for him alone. Don't laugh; the title had no trace of irony in it, and he—Chen Xiansi—certainly lived up to the name without blushing. He could write the line "Paste a thousand taels of gold on your eyelids" under the topic of autumn; his imagination had wings. When God created him, he had poetized his constitution and temperament.

He was a child from a declining family, and his environment was already somewhat difficult. He was barely able to study, relying entirely on his elder brother doing some small jobs here, taking a little bit from his meager salary to support him. He also happened to have a habit of buying literary books. Novels from various authors, complete bound magazines, were lined up on his small desk, especially poetry collections, which he loved even more. Last year, he was very annoyed because he couldn't buy Dead Water, and finally spent several nights copying the entire thing into a pocket-sized booklet in neat calligraphy. This made him extremely happy. He would read it today, read it tomorrow, and whenever he came across a sentence he didn't really understand, he would come to me, explain it once, and then we would read it together again.

To be honest, it wasn't entirely my guidance that allowed him to write such good poems. He had fallen in love with poetry before I came. At that time, my "good friend," who was teaching him Mandarin, would sometimes send me his poems to look at, introducing him in the letter as, "Look, isn't his poetry well-written? This is our poet." From this, I remembered his name clearly. After I came, the first person to come to my room to talk about literature was him. From the style of this novelist to the style of that poet, from China to foreign countries, and finally dragging in some anecdotes from the literary world, if I hadn't usually paid attention to these situations, I would have been speechless and red-faced.

From then on, my small room often had his footprints. He would come at any time; sometimes, after the bedtime bell had already rung, I was busy grading papers, and he would come, perhaps with a poem by someone else, or one of his own. At this time, I would slam my pen on the inkstone, and my heart would jump out of a tedious circle. With the joy coming from the bottom of my heart, we would talk about poetry, forgetting how much time had passed, only feeling a little dry in my mouth. When I went to pour a cup of tea that I had just brewed to drink, I touched it and found that it was already too cold to drink.

After getting closer to me, the clear stream of his poetry seemed to become more lively. Every few days, he would always send several poems for me to read, and I really loved to read them. I remember once, it was already very late at night, and after reading one of his poems, (already published in the Literary Guide? I can't remember clearly anymore.) I was so happy that I jumped up and down a few times! (That beautiful sentence, I can still recite it for you now!) That night, it was raining heavily, but I didn't care, and without even taking an umbrella, I ran all the way to his dormitory. He was alone, guarding a small lamp, planning to sleep. I rushed in and took out his poem from my pocket and recited it. After reciting it, I dropped a bunch of encouraging words, turned around, pushed open the door, and ran out. When I returned to my room, I felt cold all over, my fingers like ten icicles. I lay down, and my heart was pounding. The next day, he told me that he had tossed and turned in bed all night.

Later, I introduced his poems to various magazines and supplements, and at the same time introduced him to some young enthusiasts (who have now all published poetry collections). I remember once, a friend who edited a literary supplement asked me face-to-face: "Why don't you use your real name and instead chose the pen name Chen Xiansi?" I laughed. After I told him the truth, that friend also laughed. Xiansi's poetry was originally very ethereal, but it is true that his style changed a bit after being influenced by me. "Why not let the student establish his own style?" To this friend's question, I could only respond with another laugh.

The students in this class have a tendency to make friends. Each person has his or her close friends. Xiansi and Xing were very good friends. They had been together in elementary school, and after coming here, they were even more inseparable. Xiansi's temper was like an unguided wind, blowing in whatever direction he pleased. To be honest, he was simply too childish, but realistically, he was just an eighteen-year-old boy.

Once, he came to say goodbye to me, saying that he was about to leave the school. I asked in surprise, "Why?" The answer was also very simple: he couldn't keep up with his studies! I could understand this difficulty very well. It was impossible for a middle school student to focus his energy on one thing. He said that mathematics was simply a headache, which couldn't help but remind me of the heartache I had suffered from mathematics in middle school. I had tasted this bitterness, and I comforted him with all sorts of words, trying to stabilize his heart. I said that a poet cannot only recite and write poetry; that is not enough. I managed to calm his lion-like heart. Because he was too fond of literature, he couldn't develop his studies evenly. I had heard a lot of gossip from others, and he must have heard it too. Since it was gossip, we could just ignore it.

Xing was his older brother, and should be in terms of age. They lived in the same room, studied together, and even slept with their feet touching at night. Once his childish temper flared up, it was Xing's turn to wear out his tongue. Last spring, Xing suddenly came to me, his face looking bitter. As soon as he saw me, he said, "Xiansi suddenly shaved his head yesterday and decided to become a monk." I understood that the older brother had already run out of options for him, so he came to me for this magic weapon. Why would a young man want to shave his head and become a monk? There's a little story here.

Why did he want to be a monk for no reason?

I called him to my room, rested my chin on my hand, and asked him straight away, staring at him with both eyes, but with a smile on my lips.

"……" He couldn't answer a word, and kept touching the little white cap on top of his head with his right hand, his cheeks red, wanting to laugh and wanting to cry.

"A person can't be so uncertain. Even if your affair with Miss ××× doesn't work out for the time being, you can't do this. She has always been very good to you. How can a father casually promise his daughter to a stranger? You are really too childish!"

I saw his face turn even redder. Perhaps his heart was pounding?

Really, this girl held his heart. Their friendship was very good. His literary books were often placed by her pillow. Although they were separated in different schools, his little brother happily became his little brother (this year, in addition to him and Xing, there was a small child coming in and out). The little brother became the red娘 (matchmaker) delivering letters. I heard that when her father wanted to promise his daughter to someone else, the child cried and made a big fuss at home.

There was another thing that made him sad (perhaps a curse that hastened his death?), and that was the death of his sister and father. For his dead sister, he had written several sad poems, truly very sad, and I was really afraid to read them. The dilapidated family was like fallen leaves in the autumn wind, and people gradually withered with poverty. Once, and this was said very recently, just about two months ago, I gave the composition topic "A Letter to My Father." I walked back and forth in the classroom with my hands behind my back, and everyone else was writing happy words on their textbooks. When I patrolled to the northeast corner, I suddenly found him biting his pen and crying. A sudden wave of sadness washed over me, and I couldn't help but hate myself, hating myself for giving such a topic when there were people here who had just lost their fathers. Thinking of this, I immediately made a statement to everyone: those who have lost their fathers can write to their mothers and brothers. After saying this, I secretly walked towards the front and never dared to turn my eyes to the northeast again. In the end, his letter was still written to his father, but it also described his mother—an old, sickly, and weak woman. This letter was too sad, but fortunately, his father could no longer read it.

The three years of junior high school were about to end this semester. Since he had endured until now, he would of course have to fight to the death to grab that diploma (he called it a meal ticket, telling me: graduating from junior high school is enough, my family can't afford to support me, and I need to support my family!). All sorts of subjects were like a tangled mess, pressing hard on his heart. He had always been somewhat unfamiliar with books, and how could he suddenly turn around and become a familiar friend at this time? Moreover, the hurdles of exams were one after another: weekly exams, monthly exams, school exams, provincial exams.

I hadn't seen him much in the past few months, and he hadn't sent any poems either. I knew why. A month ago, he suddenly came down automatically in the composition class. I was staring blankly at the spring sun outside the window at this time. When I saw him coming out, I asked:

"Why did you come down?"

"A bit of a headache!"

And so he went to the dormitory, his back a last time.

Two days later, someone told me that he had gone home to seek treatment. I felt that this child had probably committed another rebellious act, and that his illness was just a plausible excuse to avoid the exams. Most of his classmates guessed this as well.

A few days passed again. At a friend's wedding feast, I heard the news of his serious illness, and my heart immediately turned from joy to sorrow.

Two more days passed. One night, after watching a flood movie, a classmate suddenly ran into my room and said, "Chen Xiansi is dead!" That night, I closed my eyes tightly, seeming to be clear-headed, but his shadow flashed before my face, clear and blurry.

The next morning, I carried a heavy burden and wanted to go up to the west city to clear my mind. As soon as I stepped out of the gate, I ran into a drunk, smoking a cigarette, his eyes like two red peaches, his feet staggered by the wind, like a pair of oars in a rapid current. As soon as he saw me, he cried out, but he couldn't actually cry. I forcefully supported him to my room, put him on the bed, and covered his face with a cold towel. I was about to pour a cup of strong tea to cool down his heart fire when he suddenly started rolling around. In this situation, I dared not say words of comfort other than to accompany him in tears. He held his head in both hands, his feet gripping the edge of the bed, and the smell of alcohol permeated the small room. Before two minutes had even passed, before I could even ask someone to pour tea, he suddenly got up and wanted to leave! He had to leave! I understood that no place could calm him down at this time. He had to leave, to go from here to there, and perhaps after getting there, he would have to go to another place. I supported him, hanging my head and letting my tears fall silently on the ground, away from countless eyes. …

On the day of his burial, Xing didn't dare to go, fearing that his mother would be saddened to see him. According to other classmates who came back to report, his mother was simply crazy, asking all day long if any family had a dead female student, wanting to arrange a ghost marriage for him.

After he was buried, Xing came to my room and brought two things, one was a four-inch photograph of Xiansi that had been taken recently, which he had entrusted to Xing to give to me before he fell ill. The other was a book of poems, selected by himself, with beautiful handwriting, already in its final draft, with revisions in black ink on the blue ink text, titled "My Poems." Opening the first page, he wrote a line: "Emotions like fleeting dreams."

Xing also told me that he had always hoped to publish a book of poems when he was alive. I agreed, promising to find a way to publish it for him in the future (with a preface written by me), so that he would have a collection like the other young poets I had introduced. Xing said that if he was lucky enough to graduate, he would not study anymore. The students in the entire school repeated the phrase "What a pity for such a genius, why don't heaven let us fools die instead," and the essays written by his classmates in mourning for him were all excellent, but this time there was no book from Xing.

Loving Father

Little Alian Getting Beaten

— Pu

Dad beats me every day,

Mom scolds me every day;

Not because I'm mischievous,

Nor because Alian is disobedient;

It's just that the machines scared Dad,

Ever since the work stopped that time,

Dad learned to drink alcohol,

Once he comes home,

Nothing is right,

He grabs Alian and beats and scolds.

He scolds me for being a useless girl,

He scolds me that I will starve to death someday:

Scolding and scolding,

He first sheds bean-like tears.

Mom doesn't like to beat, only likes to scold:

Scolds me for showing off,

Scolds me for talking too much,

Scolds me to learn well,

Scolds me not to be greedy for play.

Mom doesn't care if others scold me,

But if I scold other people's moms, she scolds me.

Sometimes I get angry and hide under the thatched shed,

Dad comes looking, Mom calls,

Asks all the left neighbors,

Asks all the right neighbors:——

In the end,

Those who care for Alian are still Dad and Mom!

July 1936

The Positivity of Satirical Literature

— Lei Shiyu

What is satirical literature? In the past, there were Lin Linjun's "Advocacy of Satirical Poetry" in the four issues of "Poetry" and Zhang Xiangshan's "The Rise of Japanese Satirical Literature" published in the Shenbao Special Edition. However, recently, Zhang's "On Satirical Literature" and Bei Ou's "Two or Three Thoughts on Satirical Literature" published in the "Dongliu" Innovation issue have caught my attention. In Zhang's essay, the emergence of satirical literature and the qualitative changes it undergoes under specific historical conditions in various eras are explained in detail, but it overlooks what weapons and strategies satirical literature should grasp to address the current reality of China. As for Bei Ou's thoughts, they are even further from our requirements. He is confined to exposing and satirizing the petty bourgeoisie and Gorky's theories, without considering the distance between the development processes of the Soviet Union and China and the requirements of objective situations. Thus, he narrowed the scope of "thoughts." In fact, in such a serious situation in China, the petty bourgeoisie, who are trapped in a declining fate and the invasion of terror, must also be on their toes. They are also working for their own survival. On the united front, they will at least go from watching and cursing to participating in attacking the common enemy, but their unique volatility cannot be ignored.

Let's talk about the social basis for the emergence of satirical literature. Generally speaking, during the period of transition of the times, that is, when the existing social system itself contains the deepening of its contradictions and the various elements that give rise to its own transformation are increasingly surfacing, one party is desperately struggling to continue its dying breath, and in order to prevent "transformation" and eliminate "transformation," it does not hesitate to use cruel political means. At such times, literature, as one of the elements of "transformation," often adopts the form of satire as a side attack to avoid frontal conflict. For example, the pungent satire of the German poet Heine and the venomous satire of the Russian poet Belinsky cause the enemy to feel pain from the bone marrow. But there are also those who belong to the ruling class, deeply feeling the powerlessness of the powerful and the increasing decline, corruption, and ugliness of their class, and adopt cynical, sentimental exposure as an elegy-like alarm bell, such as Molière and Gogol. But even more standing on the opposite position, those of the declining class who are still remaining feel uncomfortable with the new social organization and the new reality of life, and recall the old dreams of the past, fantasizing about the reproduction of the social system or that way of life, and as a result, fall into a more pitiful tragic situation, using ridicule as their elegy, the most prominent being Cervantes' "Don Quixote" in the seventeenth century. And even more wonderful and sharp are the recent masterpieces by Soviet writers Ilya Ilf and Yevgeny Petrov, such as "The Twelve Chairs" and "The Little Golden Calf."

Although it is said that "satire" originates from "laughter," this "laughter" is organized, spiritual, and technical laughter. Only in this way can it express a special kind of "satire" art in literature. Moreover, it is obvious that this art, with the passage of history and the repeated changes of social systems, has undergone changes and developments in its content and form. In particular, as a literary weapon we are currently adopting, it has special efficacy. This efficacy, needless to say, requires new creations based on our objective special conditions.

The so-called new creation is to emphasize the positivity of the theme in satire and the sharpness of the theme of satire. In the reality of our melting pot, there is no appearance of the funny character of "Don Quixote," nor does it flow out of Gogol's passive tearful cynicism, nor does it reach the leisurely, heated ridicule of Ilf et al. It is a sharp, vigorous, armed satire that forges a healthy spirit of resistance. Not only will the current biggest enemy suffer bone-piercing bee stings, but all conspirators wearing masks will also fully expose their pitiful appearances under the strong reflection of the demon-revealing mirror, and even more so, like enemy planes attacking at night being scanned by searchlights everywhere and countered by anti-aircraft guns, only in this way can satirical literature express its positivity and realize its current stage of mission.

Shenbao Local Supplement

Talk

Peace and War

— Meng Ruo

The smell of gunpowder permeates the world, and the outbreak of the Second World War is only waiting for the burning of the fuse. However, while countries are preparing for war, the peace movement is not lost because of it. Yesterday, American peace envoy Mr. Todd came to China to persuade us to join the world peace movement. According to him, the movement advocates four points: (1) The sanctity of treaties, but China has the right to amend them; (2) Limiting and reducing armaments, and eliminating the profits of manufacturing munitions; (3) Strengthening the League of Nations, so that the solidarity of the union and the power of mutual assistance will be more effective and can oppose aggression; (4) Establishing a committee in the League of Nations that will exist permanently to resolve and alleviate international tensions and prevent war from breaking out.

The peace movement is not only beyond reproach, but also deeply worthy of approval, but this movement does not have much power at present and is in vain and futile. Because countries around the world are running on the road to war, and peace can only be arranged by force. Even if we cry out for peace, we cannot compete with the loudness of the killing sound. If the peace movement can really prevent the outbreak of war, militarism would have no place to use its force. The four propositions of the world peace movement are correct. But who is willing to implement them? The sacred treaty has become a waste of paper. The League of Nations has also lost its original power. This is the result of being trampled by force, and I am afraid that the peace movement cannot recover it. Originally, war has its causes, and war is unavoidable before the causes are eliminated. People who advocate peace should see this clearly.

American historian Ransom attributed the last World War to the following four causes: (1) Nationalism and territorial recoveryism; (2) Militarism and military alliances; (3) Economic opposition and imperialism; (4) International anarchy and secret diplomacy. This was the situation in 1914, but what is it like today? These reasons can be said to still exist. We don't want to waste more words on this matter. The fact is the best explanation. The driving force of war is taking effect, and the great catastrophe of mankind will soon come. In this crisis, it is conceivable that the peace movement will have little effect.

However, it is not absolutely hopeless for the world to maintain peace. Ransom said: If countries can eliminate the evils, injustices, and mistakes of the past, forget old hatreds and start over, the happiness of the future will be unlimited. We can also say that as long as a group of ambitious people abandon their aggressive behavior, the world will be peaceful. Unfortunately, this is just a luxury for those who advocate peace. War, in the eyes of some people, may be divinely ordained. Otherwise, why is the world shaking again under the threat of cannons?

Impressions of Shanghai Orphanage (Part 2)

— Fang Zhou

He led me into a conference room, specially ordered people to brew three cups of fine Mao tea, and then said very modestly: "Our hospital is run very imperfectly, and many inappropriate places still need to be corrected!"

The hospital was founded in the thirty-first year of Guangxu, and it has a history of more than 30 years; so far, it has taken in a total of more than 2,000 orphans of both sexes, and about 400 have graduated and left the hospital. At present, the hospital still has more than 400 orphans and more than 90 orphan girls, the youngest being eight or nine years old and the oldest being eighteen years old. The education part inside is a complete elementary school, divided into six grades, with a total of four classrooms; grades one and two have full-day classes, and grades three, four, five, and six are part-time work and study. Orphans graduate after six years, and after graduation, they are either taken back by their families or introduced to a job by the hospital. Among them, those who are gifted and promising are sent by the hospital to Xiangshan Orphanage or Shanghai Nanyang Middle School. Most of the graduates of the hospital are now serving in the business world, followed by military, medical, agricultural, industrial, newspaper, and postal circles.

In terms of curriculum, in addition to elementary school education, they must also learn various crafts, so that each orphan has a skill after leaving the hospital, so that they can make a living in society in the future. The current hospital has eleven types of art (including painting, sculpture, and other beautiful works), music, printing, binding, rattan work, bamboo work, carpentry, gardening, sewing, and embroidery, and sock knitting. However, girls only learn three courses: sewing, embroidery, and sock knitting. Except for embroidery, which is contracted by others, sewing and sock knitting are for the orphans in the hospital to use themselves.

The procedures for orphans to enter the hospital are very simple. Any poor and cold children only need to register at the hospital in advance. If there is a vacancy in the hospital, then first fill out a guarantee form and send it to the hospital. After the hospital directors approve it, they can be sent there. After entering the hospital, all the necessities of life, clothing, food, and housing are provided by the hospital, but the hospital does not charge any fees, and people are free to donate as much as they want.

There are currently eleven teachers, several technicians, seven staff members, and four nannies in the hospital, all of whom are semi-voluntary, and the arrangement of hospital affairs and the cleaning of various places are entirely served by orphans in rotation.

Page 22

Now the hospital consumes more than three stones of rice per day. Usually, some of the vegetables are picked from their own garden, but they still have to buy several loads of vegetables from outside every day. They usually have meat four times a month, and every Sunday is the day for meat. The hospital's monthly operating expenses are 2,450 yuan, and about 30,000 yuan per year, of which 60% is food expenses.

The hospital has no basic funds and no subsidies from any party. The operating expenses are entirely maintained by donations from all walks of life and the hospital directors. However, in addition, the hospital also has a part of industrial production, about 2,000 yuan per year, which can also subsidize the hospital's economic shortage.

Some of the various handicrafts produced there are wholesaled, and some are displayed and sold at the entrance of the hospital.

Students with excellent grades in art are also rewarded by the hospital as usual, and the band that goes out to respond to invitations also gets a discount.

Mr. Zhang stood up and said to us:

"Now please go inside and visit as you like, but at the moment because it is a holiday, everything is very messy, and many of the orphans have gone home."

The air in the hospital is very good, and the environment is very quiet: the whole hospital has 48 buildings and 32 bungalows, covering an area of about 20 acres, and the vegetable garden covers an area of about 10 acres. We followed a corridor past, first visited the office, library, medical room, grades one and two classrooms, grades three and four classrooms, grades five classroom, grades six classroom, and then went to visit their workshops. The bamboo work department is opposite the rattan work department, and the fine arts department is next to the indoor playground. Outside is the printing department (including lithography, etc.), and the binding department is attached here. Going out from the back is the horticulture department; in front is a large open-air playground, and opposite the playground is the dining hall. The dining hall is divided into four halls, each hall can accommodate 200 people, and each hall has a hall name plaque personally inscribed by Mr. Wang Yiting. Next to the dining hall is the music department. The carpentry department is outside. The girls' department is next to the reception room, and it is completely separated from the boys' department. There are more than a dozen houses inside, and the embroidery, sewing, and sock knitting classrooms are attached here. Each department has a technician in charge of teaching, and the students are all buried in their work. The hospital is quiet and very orderly and solemn.

As for the lives of the students in the hospital, their daily life, getting up and resting are all on time. When they are sick, they are treated by the hospital doctor if they are mildly ill, and their families are notified to send them to the hospital if they are seriously ill. They usually have three meals a day, porridge in the morning, and rice for lunch and dinner.

The lower floor of the hospital building is the workshop classroom, and the upper floor is all their dormitory. After visiting around, the general situation is like this.

Waiting for Business

—

Coal Slag

— Zhi Fu

In the wilderness, in the outer circle of the city; among those who live in thatched sheds, the hot weather is too stagnant. When the sun presses down from the sky, people seem to fall into an iron furnace with a strangely high temperature, listening to the scorching of the heat wave.

At night, if the sky has a few gusts of wind, great! People are like pupae after the awakening of insects, crawling out of the door one by one, scattered like meteors in the expanded wilderness, on the road, with sewage flowing by the pool.

That's when it's lively.

Liu Rong,——an old resident who has lived near the corner of the alley for more than ten years. He lives like this, supporting a family of four.

Every evening, they start most of their work. He himself sorts out the old things he picked up during the day; Mother Rong sews and mends needlework. Let Axi, Little Jinzi roll in the garbage dump to pick up the coal blocks they picked up next to the factory.

The adults always tighten their brows and devote all their energy to work, keeping silent.

Only the two children, because the coal blocks were not picked evenly, quarreled with each other, often stomping their feet and jumping wildly, scolding: grabbing a handful of rotten coal slag and throwing it over. "Wow! Little devil..."

The little one cried, but Axi was frightened by his dark face, like a guilty criminal, standing silently in the corner of the house like a Buddha.

"Don't cry! He's not good,...uh! Let me beat him!... "Dad loves everyone, will he really whip Axi?

Fortunately, these two children are willing to obey, and after a while, they forget everything and become affectionate again.

"Little Jinzi! Where are we going tomorrow?... The place today! Too bad, I'm afraid there won't be any more..."

"...Then still go to the rails! This side..."

Little Jinzi rolled his flexible eyes, indicating that he still had to consider:

"No! Someone interferes here..."

"Is it good next to the flour mill?"

"Tch! There's only coal slag there! What do you pick it up for?"

"Coal slag..." Axi hated this thing the most in his mind, and he also cursed it fiercely.

The night deepened, the sound was quiet, the two little children had worked hard all day, and at the moment they were a little hazy, it was time to go to sleep!

Tomorrow, I have to leave the house earlier than my father, ready to find coal blocks.

One day, two days... the heat wave tightly pressed people, still as before. However, the big factories are precisely because it is summer; the shutdowns are shut down, and those who are unable to maintain are closed down. The whistle of the factory building is not as close and loud as before. It is difficult to be disturbed by a few sounds in the morning. However, the coal blocks are decreasing day by day, and even coal slag cannot be touched by people's feet everywhere.

Axi and Little Jinzi were anxious. The stable income of five or six hundred coins a day has now been discounted, and for a few days, even a day's search does not get a return.

It is also difficult for Liu Rong to rely on himself to cross the river to find work every day. Recently, he also wanted to avoid it for a while in the middle of the day because of the summer heat, but the whip of life was knocking on him invisibly, how could he not be afraid?

"What to do, there are no coal blocks lately! You..."

That night, Liu Rong came back and put a shallow basket in the corner of the wall, he sighed. Mother Rong looked sad, stepped back and fell on the bamboo couch without opening her mouth.

Axi's small face was swollen, and the right face was larger than the other side.

"Dad! Today Little Jinzi went to the coal pile stack, and while no one was there, he... he held a piece.... I knew someone rushed out halfway, he... he grabbed me and beat me... I took three slaps from him, my brother is agile... he didn't..." Axi complained, holding his swollen face:

"You...! You have to be honest! Don't do this... be brave,"

"Dad! Tomorrow we are going to pick up coal slag, there are coal chips in the coal slag, which can be sold to people to start a fire,... but, the price is not high!"

"That's good too!"

Liu Rong couldn't help but let two drops of water fall to the dry, crusty skin. His throat was choked, and his voice was low and not loud, like he had a bad cold...

In the thatched shed, everything else was as quiet as if it were surprised. All there was was the miserable sigh of their family of four.

Sing a song. Learn to fly. No one can control you. Sometimes east, sometimes west. The most free is you.

Happy and carefree. Satisfying. Now locked in a cage. Where is your innocence? Flying up doesn't touch the sky. Flying down doesn't bury the ground. Year after year, month after month, moment after moment, I have suffered the taste of iron windows. Little bird, don't call. Little bird, don't chirp. You should not
